1.0   Introduction  
BA  Group  has  been  retained  by  Stafford  Homes  Ltd.  to  examine  the  potential  traffic  impact  of  a  
proposed  residential  development  on  the  property  situated  on  the  northeast  corner  of  the  O'Connor  
Drive  /  Bermondsey  Road  /  Yardley  Avenue  intersection  in  the  City  of  Toronto  (former  Borough  of  
East  York).    Figure  1  shows  the  relationship  of  the  site  to  the  area  road  network.    
  
The  subject  site,  which  has  an  area  of  approximately  3,538.2  m2  (38,085.2  ft2),  is  located  on  the  east  
side  of  O'Connor  Drive  immediately  north  of  Yardley  Avenue  in  the  Woodbine  Gardens  
neighbourhood  (Ward  31).    Existing  land  uses  in  the  site  environs  include  single  family  residential  
dwellings  to  the  east,  Yardley  Avenue  to  the  south  with  an  auto  repair  business  beyond,  a  car  wash  /  
auto  repair  business  to  the  north  and  O'Connor  Drive  to  the  west  with  retail  and  retail  stores  beyond.  
  
A  large  multi-function  building  (O'Connor  Bowl)  occupies  the  site.    O'Connor  Bowl  has  been  a  fixture  
on  O'Connor  Drive  for  over  50  years.    This  entertainment  facility  which  is  open  to  the  public,  
accommodated  bowling  (24  lanes),  banquets,  birthday  parties,  Christmas  functions,  etc.    Vehicular  
access  to  the  public  roads  is  currently  provided  via  a  full  movement  access  driveway  onto  O'Connor  
Drive  and  a  full  movements  access  driveway  onto  Yardley  Avenue.    
  
  
1.1      Development  Proposal  
Stafford  Homes  is  proposing  to  demolish  the  existing  building  and  construct  a  new  residential  
apartment  building.    Figure  2  shows  the  Site  Plan  prepared  by  Turner  Fleischer  Architects  Inc.    Key  
elements  of  the  development  proposal  are  as  follows:  
  
x       The  development  proposal  contemplates  a  10­storey  condominium  apartment  building  with  
        196  dwelling  units,  of  which  19  units  will  be  live  /  work.      
  
x       Vehicular  access  to  the  boundary  roads  will  be  provided  via  a  two-way  driveway  onto  Yardley  
        Avenue  at  the  southeast  corner  of  the  site.    A  three-level  underground  parking  garage  with  
        approximately  220  parking  spaces  is  proposed  to  accommodate  parking  need  for  the  site.  A  
        total  of  148  bicycle  parking  spaces  are  proposed,  118  spaces  for  residential  and  live  work  
        units,  and  30  bicycle  parking  spaces  for  visitors.  
  
x       Site  loading  and  garbage  collection  facilities  are  proposed  at  grade  level  at  the  rear  of  the  
        proposed  building.    Garbage  collection  for  the  development  will  be  carried  out  at  this  
        centralized  facility.  
  
    
1.2      Study  Approach  
Study  area  intersections  are  as  follows:  
  
x       O'Connor  Drive  /  Bermondsey  Road  /  Yardley  Avenue  signalized  intersection;  
x       O'Connor  Drive  /  Dohme  Avenue  signalized  intersection;  
x       Victoria  Park  Avenue  /  Yardley  Avenue  /  Bassett  Avenue  signalized  intersection;  
x       O'Connor  Drive  /  Amsterdam  Avenue  unsignalized  intersection;  




         O'CONNOR TIS                                                                                                       1
         7009-09, February, 2012
x         Yardley  Avenue  /  Westview  Boulevard  unsignalized  intersection;  
x         Amsterdam  Avenue  /  Westview  Boulevard  unsignalized  intersection;  and    
x         Yardley  Avenue  /  Site  Access  unsignalized  intersection.    
  
A  5-year  planning  horizon,  i.e.,  horizon  year  2016,  was  selected  for  analysis  purposes.    Allowances  
were  made  for  growth  in  traffic  volumes  along  the  boundary  roads  over  the  planning  horizon.  Existing  
(2011)  traffic  conditions,  future  background  conditions  at  2016  (without  site  traffic  volumes)  and    
future  total  traffic  conditions  at  2016  (with  site  traffic  volumes)  were  analyzed.  
  
Traffic  analyses  were  focused  on  the  weekday  morning  and  afternoon  peak  hours,  since  these  hours  
represent  peak  conditions  for  both  adjacent  street  traffic  and  site  traffic.      
  
Subsequent  sections  of  this  report  deal  with  the  nature  of  existing  traffic  operations  on  the  boundary  
roads,  forecast  traffic  patterns  in  the  site  environs,  future  traffic  operations  and  any  required  
improvements  /  mitigation  measures.  
  
This  report  documents  the  results  of  analyzing  the  potential  traffic  impact  of  the  subject  
development.  
  
  
  




         O'CONNOR TIS                                                                                                     2
         7009-09, February, 2012
2.0   Existing  Transportation  Conditions  
2.1      Existing  Road  Network  
The  existing  road  network  illustrated  on  Figure  1  is  categorized  according  to  City  of  Toronto's  Road  
Classification  System  ­  Ward  31  map,  adopted  by  City  Council  June  19,  20  and  22,  2007.    
    
Major  arterial  roads  nearest  to  the  site  include  Eglinton  Avenue  which  is  located  to  the  north  of  the  
subject  site  and  facilitates  east  /  west  traffic  movement  across  the  City.      
  
Victoria  Park  Avenue  is  a  City  of  Toronto  major  arterial  roadway  located  to  the  east  of  the  subject  site  
and  facilitates  north  /  south  traffic  movements.  It  extends  from  Queen  Street  East  to  Steeles  Avenue  
East  at  the  north  limit  of  the  City.  
  
O'Connor  Drive  is  a  City  of  Toronto  major  arterial  road  located  immediately  adjacent  to  the  site.    It  
facilitates  east  /  west  traffic  movements  between  Broadview  Avenue  and  Woodbine  Avenue.    North  
of  Woodbine  Avenue,    O'Connor  Drive  runs  northeast  and  terminates  at  Victoria  Park  Avenue.      
O'Connor  Drive  has  a  basic  four  lane  urban  cross  section  with  exclusive  left  turn  lanes  at  signalized  
intersections.    Daily  traffic  volumes  on  major  arterial  roads  within  the  City  are  greater  than  20,000  
vehicles.  
  
Bermondsey  Road  is  a  City  of  Toronto  minor  arterial  road.    It  extends  northwest  from  O'Connor  Drive  
to  Eglinton  Avenue  East.    It  has  a  basic  two  lane  urban  cross  section  from  O'Connor  Drive  to  Hollinger  
Road  and  a  four  lane  cross  section  from  Hollinger  Road  to  Eglinton  Avenue.    Daily  traffic  volumes  on  
minor  arterial  roads  typically  range  from  8,000  to  20,000  vehicles.    
  
Yardley  Avenue  is  City  of  Toronto  local  road  which  extends  east  /  west  between  O'Connor  Drive  and  
Victoria  Park  Avenue.    It  has  basic  two-lane  urban  cross  section.    Traffic  calming  measures,  i.e.,    speed  
humps,  all-way  stop  control  at  mid  block  intersections  (Barron  Road  and  at  Glenburn  Avenue)  and  a  
reduction  in  the  posted  speed,  have  been  installed  along  Yardley  Avenue  between  Westview  
Boulevard  and  Victoria  Park  Avenue.    The  posted  speed  on  Yardley  Avenue  is  30  Km/h.    
  
Amsterdam  Avenue  is  City  of  Toronto  local  road  which  extends  east  /  west  between  O'Connor  Drive  
and  Victoria  Park  Avenue.    It  has  basic  two-lane  urban  cross  section.    The  posted  speed  on  Amsterdam  
Avenue  is  40  Km/h  
  
Westview  Boulevard  is  City  of  Toronto  local  road  which  extends  northeast  /  southwest  between  St.  
Clair  Avenue  and  Holland  Avenue.    It  has  a  basic  two-lane  urban  cross  section.    The  posted  speed  on  
Westview  Boulevard  south  of  Yardley  Avenue  is  30  Km/h.  
  
Existing  lane  arrangements  and  other  traffic  control  features  on  the  road  network  are  illustrated  on  
Figure  3.  




         O'CONNOR TIS                                                                                                          3
         7009-09, February, 2012
2.2               Existing  Traffic  Volumes  
2.2.1   Existing  Traffic  Volumes  
Existing  peak  hour  traffic  volume  counts  and  traffic  signal  timing  plans  for  the  study  area  signalized  
intersections  were  obtained  from  the  City  of  Toronto.    Existing  peak  hour  volumes  from  the  City  of  
Toronto  were  recorded  during  a  series  of  traffic  counts  undertaken  in  October  2007.      
  
BA  Group  also  undertook  turning  movement  counts  at  the  study  area  intersections  and  driveways  on  
January  19,  2011  during  the  weekday  am  and  pm  peak  hours.    Existing  traffic  volumes  are  illustrated  
in  Figure  4.    Existing  count  data  and  signal  timing  plans  are  provided  in  Appendix  A.  
  
  
2.2.2   Yardley  Avenue  ­  Existing  Conditions  
Existing  traffic  volumes  on  Yardley  Avenue  east  of  Westview  Boulevard  and  east  of  O'Connor  Drive  
are  illustrated  in  Exhibit  1  and  Exhibit  3,  respectively.    Existing  traffic  volumes  on  Yardley  Avenue  are  
based  upon  a  series  of  traffic  counts  conducted  by  BA  Group  in  June  2011.    Hourly  traffic  volumes  
throughout  the  busiest  day,  i.e.,  Tuesday,  are  illustrated  in  Exhibit  2  and  Exhibit  4,  respectively.    
  
The  results  indicate  that,  daily  traffic  volumes  on  Yardley  Avenue  east  of  Westview  Boulevard  range  
from  1715  to  1865  vehicles  during  the  week  (1100  to  1290  vehicles  on  the  weekend).    Between  
O'Connor  Drive  and  Westview  Boulevard,  daily  traffic  volumes  on  Yardley  Avenue  range  from  4010  to  
4360  vehicles  during  the  week  (2956  to  3442  vehicles  on  the  weekend).    We  note  that  through  a  
typical  weekday,  traffic  volumes  on  Yardley  Avenue  east  of  Westview  Boulevard  are  approximately  1  
vehicle  every  25  seconds  around  8:00  am  and  approximately  1  vehicle  every  20  seconds  between  3:00  
pm  and  6:00  pm.

                                                                                                  2-Way Traffic




2.3              Intersection  Operations  
2.3.1     Signalized  Intersections  
Traffic  operations  at  the  signalized  intersections  were  analyzed  using  the  procedures  set  out  in  the  
City  of  Toronto  "Guidelines For Using Synchro 7 (Including SimTraffic 7)"  
dated  April  22,  2010,  with  the  assistance  of  Trafficware  Traffic  Signal  Timing  software  ­  Synchro.      
Signal  cycle  lengths  and  timing  plans  currently  in  effect  at  the  intersections  were  obtained  from  the  
City  of  Toronto.    Synchro  reports  for  existing  traffic  conditions  are  provided  in  Appendix  B.        
  
Table  1  summarizes  the  performance  results.  Indicators  for  measuring  the  performance  of  signalized  
intersections  are  volume-to-capacity  (v/  c)  ratios,  level  of  service  (LOS)  and  delay,  where  a  v/c  ratio  of  
1.0  indicates  `at  or  near  capacity'  conditions.    Capacity  analysis  summary  worksheets  are  attached  in  
Appendix  B.  
  
Existing  conditions  at  the  O'Connor  /  Dohme  intersection  reflect  good  levels  of  service  with  LOS  A  
(v/c  of  0.33  and  0.38)  during  the  am  and  pm  peak  hours,  respectively.    Existing  conditions  at    the  
O'Connor  /  Bermondsey  /  Yardley  intersection  reflect  good  level  of  service  with  LOS  B  (v/c  of  0.53  
and  0.52)  during  the  am  and  pm  peak  hours,  respectively.    Existing  conditions  at    the  Victoria  Park  /  
Yardley  intersection  reflect  good  levels  of  service  with  LOS  A  (v/c  of  0.28  and  0.37)  during  the  am  and  
pm  peak  hours,  respectively.

summarizes  the  performance  results.

2.3       Public  Transit  Service  
As  illustrated  in  the  map  below,  the  70A  and  70B  O'Connor  bus  routes  operate  between  Coxwell  
Subway  Station  and  the  area  of  Eglinton  Avenue  East  and  Pharmacy  Avenue,  generally  in  an  east-west  
direction.    The  70A  (Coxwell  Station­Eglinton  Square)  branch  operates  until  approximately  9:00  pm,  
seven  days  a  week.  The  70B  (Coxwell  Station­Eglinton  Square)  short-turn  branch  operates  during  the  
late  evening  only,  seven  days  a  week.      Far  side  bus  stop  and  shelter  are  provided  on  the  east  side  of  
O'Connor  Drive  immediately  in  front  of  the  subject  site.    Near  side  bus  stop  and  shelter  are  provided  
on  the  west  side  of  O'Connor  Drive  across  from  the  site.  




                                                                                       
Toronto  Transit  Commission  (TTC)  Bus  Routes  70A  &  70B  O'Connor  
(Source  TTC  Website,  July  2011)  
  




          O'CONNOR TIS                                                                                                             8
          7009-09, February, 2012
3.0   Traffic  Volume  Forecast  
3.1            Future  Background  Traffic  Volumes  
A  five=year  planning  horizon  (year  2016)  has  been  selected  as  an  appropriate  time  frame  within  
which  the  proposed  development  may  be  constructed  and  fully  occupied.      
  
Annual  growth  rates  for  the  traffic  volume  changes  were  derived  based  upon  a  review  of  historical  24-
hour  traffic  volumes  obtained  from  Toronto  Transportation  Services  Traffic  Safety  Unit  for  the  years  
2003  through  2008  on  O'Connor  Drive  and  Bermondsey  Road.    For  the  purposes  of  this  study  a  
growth  rate  of  1.5%  per  year  compounded  was  applied  to  existing  traffic  volumes  over  5  years.        
These  increases  were  applied  to  all  movements  (through  and  turning)  at  the  signalized  intersections.      
  
Forecast  traffic  volumes  that  would  be  generated  by  the  approved  but  not  yet  completed  
development  at  23  to  27  Hobson  Avenue  were  also  included  as  background  traffic.    Site  traffic  
volumes  for  the  Hobson  Avenue  residential  development  were  extracted  from  the  traffic  impact  study  
report  prepared  by  BA  Group  in  March  31,  2008.  
      
Future  background  traffic  volumes  illustrated  in  Figure  5  were  therefore  calculated  by  factoring  up  
existing  traffic  volumes  on  the  boundary  roads  and  by  adding  traffic  volumes  generated  by  other  
developments  in  the  area.

reports  for  future  background  traffic  conditions  are  provided  in  Appendix  C.  
  
Future  background  traffic  may  result  in  a  modest  impact  (2  and  9  percent  increases)  on  the  overall  v/c  
ratios  at  the  O'Connor  Street  /  Dohme  intersection,  (6  and  1  percent  increases)  on  the  O'Connor  /  
Bermondsey  intersection  and  (1  and  3  percent  increases)  on  the  Victoria  Park  /  Yardley  intersection  
during  the  am  and  pm  peak  hours,  respectively.    Good  levels  of  traffic  operation  are  maintained  under  
future  background  traffic  conditions.

4.1.1   O'Connor  Street  Intersections  
Site  traffic  will  have  minimal  impact  (1%  increase)  on  the  overall  v/c  ratio  at  the  O'Connor  /  Dohme  
intersection  during  pm  peak  hour.    This  intersection  will  continue  to  operate  at  good  levels  of  service,  
LOS  `A'  overall  with  v//c  ratios  of  0.35  and  0.43  during  both  peak  hours.      
  
Site  traffic  will  have  modest  impact  (7%  increase)  on  the  overall  v/c  ratios  at  the  O'Connor  /  
Bermondsey  /  Yardley  intersection  during  am  peak  hour.    The  O'Connor  /  Bermondsey  /  Yardley  
intersection  will  continue  to  operate  at  good  levels  of  service,  LOS  `B'  overall  with  v//c  ratios  of  0.65  
and  0.59  during  both  peak  hours.      
  
Therefore,  under  future  total  traffic  conditions,  the  O'Connor  Drive  intersections  can  be  expected  to  
operate  with  good  operational  characteristics  with  no  critical  movements  and  significant  overall  
reserve  capacity.    
  
  
4.1.2   Victoria  Park  Avenue  Intersection  
Site  traffic  will  have  minimal  impact  (1%  increase)  on  the  overall  v/c  ratio  at  the  Victoria  Park  /  
Yardley  intersection  during  am  peak  hour.    The  Victoria  Park  /  Yardley  intersection  will  continue  to  
operate  at  very  good  levels  of  service,  LOS  `A'  overall  with  v//c  ratios  of  0.30  and  0.40  during  the  am  
and  pm  peak  hours,  respectively.

expected  to  operate  with  good  operational  characteristics  with  no  critical  movements  and  significant  
overall  reserve  capacity.  
  
  
4.3      Impact  on  Yardley  Avenue  
During  the  am  and  pm  peak  hours,  the  proposed  residential  development  will  add  approximately  5  
and  3  vehicles  to  peak  hour  traffic  volumes  on  Yardley  Avenue  east  of  Westview  Boulevard.    Daily  
volumes  on  Yardley  Avenue  east  of  Westview  Boulevard  will  continue  to  be  less  than  2,000  vehicles.      
  




         O'CONNOR TIS                                                                                                     21
         7009-09, February, 2012
5.0     Site  Plan  Evaluation  
5.1      Transportation  Demand  Management  

As  noted  previously,  the  site  has  good  transit  accessibility  with  bus  stops  and  shelters  located  on  
O'Connor  Drive  immediately  in  front  of  the  proposed  building.    Additional  Transportation  Demand  
Management  (TDM)  measures  are  proposed  to  reduce  the  reliance  on  private  automobiles  and  to  
encourage  alternative  modes  of  transportation.    These  include,  ensuring  no  oversupply  of  parking  
spaces,  provision  of  adequate  bicycle  parking  based  upon  relevant  performance  criteria,  integration  of  
pedestrian  connections  to  the  existing  transit  stops  and  shelters.        
  
  
5.2      Site  Automobile  Parking  Provisions  
The  applicable  Zoning  By-Law  (former  Borough  of  East  York  By-Law  6752)  parking  standard  for  the  
multi  unit  apartment  buildings  is  1.0  parking  space  /  dwelling  unit.    Based  upon  this  By-Law  standard,  
a  total  of  196  parking  spaces  are  required  for  the  project.      
  
Draft  By-law  1156-2010  which  has  recently  been  repealed  by  the  City  of  Toronto  for  further  study,  
contains  technical  parking  criteria  based  upon  updated  survey  results.    It  also  provides  a  more  detailed  
assessment  of  the  parking  requirements  for  residential  developments  on  Avenues  well  served  by  
surface  transit.    We  note  that  O'Connor  Drive  between  Sandra  Avenue  and  Victoria  Park  Avenue  is  
designated  as  an  Avenue  in  the  City's  Official  Plan.    
  
Therefore,  the  proposed  minimum  resident  and  visitor  parking  standards  for  the  development  are  as  
follows:  
         x         Bachelor  Units                                 0.70  spaces  /  unit;  
         x         One  Bedroom  Units                             0.80  spaces  /  unit;  
         x         Two  Bedroom  Units                             0.90  spaces  /  unit;  
         x         Three  Bedroom  Units                           1.10  spaces  /  unit;  and  
         x         Visitor  Parking                                0.15  spaces  /  unit.  
  
Assuming  all  dwelling  units  will  be  two-bedroom  units,  a  total  of  206  parking  spaces  would  be  
required  for  the  subject  development.    Approximately  220  parking  will  be  provided  in  a  common  
underground  parking  garage.    
  
Therefore,  the  proposed  parking  supply  is  thus  appropriate  and  supportive  of  the  identified  TDM  
objectives.    
  
  
5.3      Site  Bicycle  Parking  Provisions  
The  Toronto  Green  Standards  (revised  December  31,  2010)  form  part  of  the  comprehensive  
performance  standards  that  are  considered  to  support  sustainable  development  objectives  for  new  
development  in  the  City.    Based  upon  Green  Standards  criteria,  a  total  of  118  bicycle  parking  spaces  
are  required  /  provided  for  residential  and  live  work  units  based  upon  a  rate  of  0.6  spaces  per  unit,  and  
30  bicycle  parking  spaces  are  required  /  provided  for  visitors  at  a  rate  of  0.15  spaces  per  dwelling  unit.  
Site  bicycle  parking  provisions  are  thus  appropriate  and  supportive  of  the  TDM  objectives.  




         O'CONNOR TIS                                                                                                            22
         7009-09, February, 2012
6.0   Summary  and  Conclusions  
BA  Group  has  examined  the  traffic  implications  of  a  proposed  residential  development  on  the  
O'Connor  Bowl  site.    The  proposed  development  plan  contemplates  a  total  of  196  residential  units  
including  19  live  /  work  units.    The  subject  lands  are  generally  located  at  the  northeast  corner  of  
O'Connor  Drive  /  Bermondsey  Road  /  Yardley  Avenue  signalized  intersection  in  the  City  of  Toronto  
(former  Borough  of  East  York).  
  
Vehicular  access  will  be  provided  via  a  full  movement  access  driveway  onto  Yardley  Avenue,  located  
at  the  southeast  limit  of  the  subject  property.    
  
Key  findings  are  as  follows:  
  
x         The  subject  development  is  well  located  with  respect  to  the  major  area  road  network.    Site  
          traffic  will  be  effectively  distributed  in  the  four  cardinal  directions  --  east  and  west  along  
          Bermondsey  Road  /  Yardley  Avenue  and  north  and  south  along  O'Connor  Drive.    The  proposed  
          residential  development  is  also  afforded  a  high  degree  of  transit  accessibility.      
  
x         Existing  conditions  at  the  O'Connor  Drive  /  Dohme  Avenue,  O'Connor  Drive  /  Bermondsey  
          Road  /  Yardley  Avenue  and  Victoria  Park  Avenue  /  Yardley  Avenue  signalized  intersections  
          reflect  good  levels  of  service,  LOS  `A',  `B'  and  `A',  respectively,  during  both  peak  hours.  
  
x         With  ongoing  growth  in  boundary  road  traffic  along  O'Connor  Drive,  Victoria  Park  Avenue,  
          Bermondsey  Road,  Dohme  Avenue  and  Yardley  Avenue,  the  signalized  intersections  will  
          continue  to  operate  at  good  levels  of  service  LOS  `A',  `B'  and  `A'.    There  will  be  modest  
          increases  (1%  to  6%  in  the  am  peak  hour  and  1%  to  9%  during  the  pm  peak  hour)  on  v/c  
          ratios.    Significant  reserve  capacity  will  be  available  at  the  intersections  to  accommodate  site  
          generated  traffic  volumes.    
  
x         The  proposed  development  will  generate  approximately  85  trips  during  the  a.m.  peak  hour  (15  
          vehicles  inbound  and  70  vehicles  outbound)  and  80  trips  during  the  pm  peak  hour  (50  vehicles  
          inbound  and  30  vehicles  outbound).          
  
x         Site  traffic  will  have  minimal  (1%  increase)  on  the  overall  v/c  ratio  at  the  O'Connor  /  Dohme  
          and  Victoria  Park  /  Yardley  intersections.    At  the  O'Connor  /Bermondsey  /  Yardley  
          intersection,  site  traffic  will  have  a  modest  impact  on  the  overall  v/c  ratio  during  the  am  peak  
          hour.    Under  future  total  traffic  conditions,  i.e.,  with  full  build  out  and  occupancy  of  the  
          development,  good  levels  of  traffic  operation  will  be  maintained  at  the  study  area  
          intersections.    
  
x         Under  existing  conditions,  all  unsignalized  intersections  in  the  boundary  road  network  are  
          currently  operating  at  good  levels  of  service  during  the  am  and  pm  peak  hours.    The  v/c  ratios  
          and  delay  are  very  low  and  indicate  that  substantial  excess  capacity  is  available  for  turning  
          traffic.    Site  traffic  will  have  minimal  impact  (1%  increases)  on  the  v/c  ratio  for  the  eastbound  
          shared  left  /right  movement  at  the  Yardley  /  Westview  intersection.    However,  good  levels  of  
          traffic  operation  will  be  maintained  at  the  unsignalized  study  area  intersections.  
  




         O'CONNOR TIS                                                                                                           23
         7009-09, February, 2012
x    The  proposed  site  access  driveway  onto  Yardley  Avenue  will  operate  at  good  levels  of  service,  
     LOS  `A'  and  `B'  during  the  am  and  pm  peak  hours.    The  driveway  is  situated  in  an  appropriate  
     location  and  is  designed  to  allow  for  ease  of  access  /  egress  for  passenger  cars  and  trucks.    
  
x    Site  vehicle  and  bicycle  parking  provisions  are  appropriate  and  supportive  of  identified  TDM  
     objectives.      
  
x    The  findings  of  the  study  indicate  that  the  traffic  generated  by  the  proposed  residential  
     development  will  not  have  any  noticeable  traffic  impact  during  the  peak  hours  and  as  a  result  
     can  be  acceptably  accommodated  on  the  area  street  network.
